# Rhodawk DevSecOps Engine — Codebase Analysis Playbook

> Generated by AST-grounded analysis. Every signature, import, class, function and constant in Part I and Part IV is extracted directly from source via the Python `ast` module (Python files), regex parsing of the Markdown / TypeScript / shell / Dockerfile syntax (everything else), and verbatim reads of configuration files. Nothing in Part I or Part IV is paraphrased.

| Method | Signature | Decorators | Docstring (first line) |

| `run_sast` | `(self, diff_text: str, changed_files: list[str], repo_dir: str) -> RuntimeSastReport` | `@abstractmethod` | Run static analysis on the AI-generated diff. |
| `run_supply_chain` | `(self, diff_text: str, repo_dir: str) -> RuntimeSupplyChainReport` | `@abstractmethod` | Audit dependencies added/changed by the AI diff. |

| `get_fix_prompt_instructions` | `(self, test_path: str, branch_name: str, src_hint: str = '') -> str` | `@abstractmethod` | Language-specific instruction block appended to Aider prompts. |
| `_run` | `(cmd: list[str], cwd: str, timeout: int = 300, extra_env: dict \| None = None, raise_on_error: bool = False) -> tuple[str, int]` | `@staticmethod` | Thin safe subprocess wrapper (shell=False enforced). |

## PART II — Vendor Section

### II-A. `vendor/openclaude/` — External Research Analysis

> The `vendor/openclaude/` directory contains the prebuilt OpenClaude TypeScript bundle and was **NOT traversed**. The analysis below comes from cross-references found in the core source tree (`Dockerfile`, `entrypoint.sh`, `openclaude_grpc/`, `openclaw_gateway.py`, `hermes_orchestrator.py`, `requirements.txt`, `.env.example`) plus the upstream project `https://github.com/Gitlawb/openclaude`.

**What OpenClaude is.** OpenClaude is an open, headless implementation of Anthropic's Claude Code coding-agent loop. Upstream it ships as a TypeScript/Bun CLI plus a gRPC headless daemon mode. It exposes a long-running coding agent that can be driven over gRPC by an external orchestrator (here, the Python brain in this repo) instead of through an interactive terminal session.

**Why this codebase uses it.** This repo embeds OpenClaude as the *code-generation lane* of its agent squad. The Python orchestrator (`hermes_orchestrator.py`, `openclaw_gateway.py`) needs a tool-using LLM agent that can read/write files, run shell commands, and invoke MCP servers without burning a real Anthropic seat — OpenClaude provides that, pointed at any OpenAI-compatible inference endpoint via `OPENAI_BASE_URL` (DigitalOcean Inference primary, OpenRouter fallback). The entrypoint launches **two** OpenClaude daemons, one per provider:

```
OPENCLAUDE_GRPC_PORT_DO = 50051   # DigitalOcean Inference (PRIMARY)
OPENCLAUDE_GRPC_PORT_OR = 50052   # OpenRouter (FALLBACK)
```

**Integration points found in the core tree:**

| Integration point | File in core codebase | How OpenClaude is used |
|-------------------|----------------------|------------------------|
| gRPC client | `openclaude_grpc/client.py` | Talks to the daemon over gRPC; stub generation in Dockerfile / `scripts/generate_stubs.sh` |
| Stub generation | `Dockerfile` (`grpc_tools.protoc`) | Reads `/opt/openclaude/src/proto/openclaude.proto` from the vendored copy |
| Process supervision | `entrypoint.sh:start_daemon` | Spawns `bun run scripts/start-grpc.ts` per provider |
| Routing | `openclaw_gateway.py` | HTTP gateway that routes EmbodiedOS commands → OpenClaude |
| Hermes provider lane | `hermes_orchestrator.py` (env `HERMES_PROVIDER=openclaude_grpc`) | Selects gRPC lane for code-generation tasks |
| Schedule | `openclaw_schedule.yaml` | Cron heartbeat for OpenClaw missions |

**What OpenClaude provides to this system.** Concretely, OpenClaude gives the Python brain a stable, file-system-aware coding agent runtime. The orchestrator does *not* implement its own diff-application, edit loop, or tool-call schema — it delegates that entirely to OpenClaude. Tasks like *patch a vulnerable function*, *generate a regression test*, *refactor a module to add input sanitization*, and *write a PoC exploit* are emitted by the Python side as gRPC calls to OpenClaude with a high-level prompt and let the daemon apply file edits in the repo workdir. If `vendor/openclaude/` were removed: (a) the Dockerfile stage `openclaude-builder` would fail because it copies from `vendor/openclaude/package.json` and `vendor/openclaude/`; (b) the runtime `protoc` step would fail because `/opt/openclaude/src/proto/openclaude.proto` would never be populated; (c) `openclaude_grpc/client.py` would still import its protobuf stubs but every RPC would fail with `UNAVAILABLE` because no daemon would be listening on `:50051`/`:50052`. The fallback in `openclaw_gateway.py` (HTTP CLI surface) and the FALLBACK lane via OpenRouter do not bring back the agent loop — they just keep the rest of the orchestrator alive.

**Trust boundary.** Data flows OUT of this repo into OpenClaude as: (1) the cloned target repo workdir mounted into `/data`, (2) prompts assembled by Hermes from RAG / SAST / fuzzing outputs, (3) MCP tool-call definitions from `mcp_config.ARCHIVE.json` and per-skill manifests. Data flowing BACK is: file edits applied to the repo workdir, JSON tool-call transcripts surfaced to `audit_logger.py`, and final patches/PR descriptions consumed by `github_app.py` / `commit_watcher.py`. OpenClaude itself reaches out to whatever `OPENAI_BASE_URL` is configured (DigitalOcean Inference or OpenRouter) — no Anthropic API is ever called from this repo.

**Vendor metadata (from .gitignore, Dockerfile, package.json visible in core tree):**

```
vendor/openclaude/ summary:
  - Files: ~2250 (NOT traversed)
  - Primary language: TypeScript / React
  - Build tool: Bun
  - Build output: dist/cli.mjs
  - Build stage name: openclaude-builder (Dockerfile line 4)
  - Runtime dependency: Bun (copied from oven/bun:latest into final image)
```

## PART III — Architecture & System Design

### III-1. System overview

Rhodawk DevSecOps Engine is a long-running, multi-agent **autonomous offensive-security and patching engine**. Its job is to ingest a target repository (pulled via a GitHub PAT), discover real, exploitable vulnerabilities in it using a stack of static, dynamic, symbolic, fuzzing, taint, and LLM-assisted techniques, then *fix* those vulnerabilities by delegating concrete code edits to a vendored OpenClaude coding-agent daemon. It surfaces results through three interfaces simultaneously: a Gradio chat UI on port 7860 (`app.py`), a FastAPI control plane (`mythos/api/fastapi_server.py`), and a GitHub App / webhook listener (`webhook_server.py`, `github_app.py`, `commit_watcher.py`).

It is operationally an **always-on container**, not a request/response API. The main process (`app.py`) is wrapped by `entrypoint.sh`, which boots: (1) the camofox-browser anti-detection browser server on `127.0.0.1:9377`, (2) one OpenClaude gRPC daemon per LLM provider, (3) the G0DM0D3 meta-learner background daemon (`meta_learner_daemon.py`), (4) Hermes orchestration and the OpenClaw HTTP gateway. A scheduler (`openclaw_schedule.yaml`) drives recurring missions: harvester runs every 6h, night-hunt at 23:00 UTC, morning report at 06:00 UTC, weekly LoRA exports, weekly training digest. Bug-bounty submission, disclosure, and OSS guardian flows are all triggered from the same orchestrator.

Primary consumers: a single human operator via Gradio/Telegram, plus the GitHub App (which talks to it on PR events). It is **not** a multi-tenant SaaS — single deployment per operator/team, persistent local state in `/data`, all model and tool credentials provided via `.env`.

```
                                     ┌────────────────────────────┐

### III-4. Data flow map — single bug-bounty audit

```
1. GitHub webhook fires    →  webhook_server.py:webhook_handler
2. HMAC verified           →  webhook_server.py:_verify_signature
3. Mission enqueued        →  job_queue.JobQueue.enqueue
4. Worker picks up job     →  worker_pool.WorkerPool._loop
5. Repo cloned             →  github_app.py:clone_repo  (PyGithub)
6. Hermes plans            →  hermes_orchestrator.HermesOrchestrator.plan
7. SAST sweep              →  sast_gate.run_all → mythos/static/{semgrep,joern,codeql}_bridge
8. Taint+chain analysis    →  taint_analyzer + chain_analyzer (semantic_extractor as input)
9. Symbolic targeting      →  symbolic_engine + formal_verifier (z3, angr)
10. Fuzzing                →  harness_factory + fuzzing_engine + red_team_fuzzer + AFL++ via mythos/dynamic
11. Dynamic probes         →  mythos/dynamic/frida_instr / gdb_automation / qemu_harness
12. Findings classified    →  vuln_classifier.classify  →  conviction_engine.score
13. Adversarial review     →  adversarial_reviewer.review  +  bugbounty_checklist.run
14. Patch generation       →  openclaude_grpc.client.OpenClaudeClient.run_task (gRPC :50051)
15. Patch verification     →  verification_loop.run + swebench_harness
16. PR opened / patch push →  github_app.py:open_pull_request
17. Disclosure recorded    →  disclosure_vault.DisclosureVault.record
18. Bounty submission      →  bounty_gateway.submit (HackerOne/Bugcrowd)
19. Operator notified      →  notifier.send + public_leaderboard.update
20. Audit chain appended   →  audit_logger.AuditLogger.append (signed chain)
21. Episode persisted      →  training_store + embedding_memory + lora_scheduler.maybe_export
```

### III-6. Concurrency & execution model

- **Process model.** Single-container, multi-process. `entrypoint.sh` background-spawns: camofox-browser (Node), one OpenClaude daemon per provider (Bun), the meta-learner daemon (Python), then `exec`s `app.py` (Python) as PID 1's foreground process.
- **Within `app.py`.** Gradio's own thread pool serves UI events. `worker_pool.py` implements a thread-based worker loop (`threading.Thread` + `queue.Queue`-equivalent backed by `job_queue.py`'s SQLite store). `webhook_server.py` runs an HTTP listener on a thread.
- **Async surface.** `mythos/api/fastapi_server.py` is an `async`/`await` FastAPI app served by `uvicorn`; the rest of the orchestrator is synchronous threads with explicit `time.sleep` polling for the few cases that need it.
- **Queue.** `job_queue.JobQueue` uses SQLite as the durable backing store with FIFO ordering; `night_hunt_lock.py` provides a single-instance lock around the night-hunt loop so two nightly runs never overlap.
- **Worker pool.** `worker_pool.WorkerPool` owns a fixed number of workers and pulls from the queue; missions are coarse (one per repo audit) so the pool size is small (single-digit).
- **Race-condition mitigations.** Filesystem locks (`night_hunt_lock`), HMAC verification before enqueue (`webhook_server`), audit chain hash linkage (`audit_logger`), idempotent OpenClaude RPCs (`openclaude_grpc/client.py` retries with backoff via `tenacity`).
- **Locking primitives.** `threading.Lock` for in-process state, file locks under `/data` for cross-process state, no Redis or distributed lock — single-node deployment by design.

## PART IV — Deep Functional Analysis (Subsystem by Subsystem)

Each subsection covers one major file or logical subsystem. Purpose, fit, classes, functions, configuration, error handling, performance, and security are all grounded in the AST data extracted in Part I.

### IV-1. `app.py`

**Purpose.** Rhodawk AI — Autonomous DevSecOps Control Plane v4.0 This module declares 0 classes and 62 top-level functions, with 36 import statements.

**How it fits.**

- Called by (intra-repo importers): _no other core file imports it (entrypoint or webhook target)._
- Calls into (intra-repo modules): `adversarial_reviewer`, `audit_logger`, `bounty_gateway`, `conviction_engine`, `embedding_memory`, `formal_verifier`, `github_app`, `hermes_orchestrator`, `job_queue`, `language_runtime`, `lora_scheduler`, `memory_engine`, `notifier`, `openclaude_grpc`, `red_team_fuzzer`, `sast_gate`, `supply_chain`, `training_store`, `verification_loop`, `vuln_classifier`, `webhook_server`, `worker_pool`

**Top-level functions.**

- `ui_log(message: str, level: str = 'INFO')` — (no docstring)
- `run_subprocess_safe(cmd: list, cwd: str = REPO_DIR, timeout: int = 300, env_overrides: dict = None, raise_on_error: bool = True) -> tuple[str, int]` — (no docstring)
- `_kill_active_processes() -> int` — (no docstring)
- `configure_git_credentials()` — Set up git credential storage.
- `write_mcp_config() -> str` — Write the full 25-server cybersecurity MCP config to /tmp/mcp_runtime.json.
- `safe_git_pull()` — (no docstring)
- `cleanup_stale_branch(branch_name: str)` — (no docstring)
- `create_fix_branch(branch_name: str) -> bool` — (no docstring)
- `ensure_fix_committed(test_path: str) -> None` — (no docstring)

## PART V — Integration Points & External Dependencies

### V-1. External API integrations

| Service | Referenced in | Auth method | Endpoints used | Failure mode |
|---------|--------------|-------------|----------------|--------------|
| GitHub REST/GraphQL | github_app.py, commit_watcher.py, repo_harvester.py, webhook_server.py | GitHub App JWT (PyJWT) + PAT (GITHUB_TOKEN) | /repos, /pulls, /issues, /webhooks | PyGithub raises; orchestrator queues for retry |
| HackerOne | bounty_gateway.py, disclosure_vault.py | HACKERONE_API_KEY + HACKERONE_USERNAME (HTTP basic) | /v1/reports, /v1/programs | Degrades silently if env unset |
| Bugcrowd | bounty_gateway.py | BUGCROWD_API_KEY (Bearer) | /v2/submissions | Degrades silently |
| NVD CVE DB | cve_intel.py | NVD_API_KEY (header) | /rest/json/cves/2.0 | Falls back to cached snapshot |
| Brave Search | knowledge_rag.py, repo_harvester.py | BRAVE_API_KEY (header) | /res/v1/web/search | Degrades to local search |
| Semgrep AppSec | sast_gate.py, mythos/static/semgrep_bridge.py | SEMGREP_APP_TOKEN | Semgrep Cloud APIs | Falls back to local semgrep CLI |
| Nuclei (ProjectDiscovery) | mythos/mcp/web_security_mcp.py + sast_gate | NUCLEI_API_KEY | Nuclei templates | Local templates only |
| Shodan | mythos/mcp/shodan_mcp.py | SHODAN_API_KEY | /shodan/host/search | Skips recon step |
| URLScan | mythos/mcp/reconnaissance_mcp.py + clientside_resources.py | URLSCAN_API_KEY | /api/v1/scan/ | Skips recon step |
| DigitalOcean Inference (PRIMARY LLM) | llm_router.py, model_squad.py, hermes_orchestrator.py, entrypoint.sh | DO_INFERENCE_API_KEY (Bearer) | /v1/chat/completions (OpenAI-compat) | Falls back to OpenRouter |
| OpenRouter (FALLBACK LLM) | llm_router.py, model_squad.py, entrypoint.sh | OPENROUTER_API_KEY (Bearer) | /api/v1/chat/completions | Surfaces error; no further fallback |
| Camofox-browser | camofox_client.py | Optional CAMOFOX_API_KEY for cookie writes | REST: /launch, /goto, /screenshot, /cookies | Returns 403 on cookie writes if no key |
| Telegram Bot API | embodied_os.py, notifier.py, openclaw_schedule.yaml | TELEGRAM_BOT_TOKEN + TELEGRAM_CHAT_ID | /sendMessage, webhook ingress | Skips channel if env unset |
| Discord / Slack | notifier.py, openclaw_schedule.yaml | DISCORD_WEBHOOK_URL / SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL | POST webhook URL | Skips channel if env unset |

### V-2. gRPC services

- `vendor/openclaude/src/proto/openclaude.proto` is the source of truth (NOT traversed). The Dockerfile compiles it into `openclaude_grpc/openclaude_pb2.py` and `openclaude_grpc/openclaude_pb2_grpc.py`.
- Server: the OpenClaude headless daemon (Bun, `bun run scripts/start-grpc.ts`).
- Clients: `openclaude_grpc/client.py` (Python) — used by `hermes_orchestrator.py` and `openclaw_gateway.py`.
- Transport: TCP, host `127.0.0.1`, ports `50051` (DigitalOcean lane) and `50052` (OpenRouter lane). No TLS (loopback only); auth is by container boundary (the daemons are not exposed).

### V-3. Webhook interfaces

- `webhook_server.py` exposes `/webhook` (POST). Verifies GitHub `X-Hub-Signature-256` HMAC (`tests/test_webhook_hmac.py` covers this), parses `event` and `payload`, and enqueues a mission via `job_queue`.
- `mythos/api/webhooks.py` exposes additional FastAPI webhook routes for the Mythos plane.
- `openclaw_gateway.py` exposes `POST /openclaw/command` (NL command intake) and a Telegram webhook receiver as defined by `openclaw_schedule.yaml:channels.telegram`.

### V-4. MCP (Model Context Protocol) configuration

- Master registry: `mcp_config.ARCHIVE.json` (508 lines). Per-domain MCP servers live under `mythos/mcp/*.py` and are loaded by `mythos/mcp/_mcp_runtime.py` (see `tests/test_mcp_servers_load.py`).
- Servers shipped: `browser_agent_mcp`, `can_bus_mcp`, `cors_analyzer_mcp`, `dep_confusion_mcp`, `dynamic_analysis_mcp`, `exploit_generation_mcp`, `frida_runtime_mcp`, `ghidra_bridge_mcp`, `httpx_probe_mcp`, `jwt_analyzer_mcp`, `openapi_analyzer_mcp`, `prototype_pollution_mcp`, `reconnaissance_mcp`, `scope_parser_mcp`, `sdr_analysis_mcp`, `shodan_mcp`, `skill_selector_mcp`, `static_analysis_mcp`, `subdomain_enum_mcp`, `vulnerability_database_mcp`, `wayback_mcp`, `web_security_mcp`.
- Externally-installed MCP servers (Dockerfile lines 47–52): `@modelcontextprotocol/server-github`, `-filesystem`, `-memory`, `-sequential-thinking`, `-brave-search`, plus Python `mcp-server-fetch`, `mcp-server-git`, `mcp-server-sqlite`.
- Transport: stdio (default for MCP); the gateway is `mythos/mcp/_mcp_runtime.py` and the orchestrator loads them via `mcp_config.ARCHIVE.json` at boot (path `MCP_RUNTIME_CONFIG=/tmp/mcp_runtime.json`).

### V-5. LLM provider integrations

| Provider | Referenced in | Models used | API-key env var | Used for |
|----------|--------------|-------------|-----------------|----------|
| DigitalOcean Inference | `llm_router.py`, `model_squad.py`, `hermes_orchestrator.py`, `entrypoint.sh` | `EXECUTION_MODEL` (default `llama-3.3-70b-instruct`), `HERMES_MODEL` (`deepseek-r1-distill-llama-70b`), `TRIAGE_MODEL` (`qwen3-32b`) | `DO_INFERENCE_API_KEY` | The Hands / Brain / Screener |
| OpenRouter | same as above | `RECON_MODEL` (`kimi-k2.5`), `FALLBACK_MODEL` (`claude-4.6-sonnet`), `FALLBACK_MODEL_ALT` (`minimax-m2.5`) | `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` | The Reader / Safety Net |

Call pattern (from `llm_router.py` and `model_squad.py`): role-aware routing (`EXECUTION` / `HERMES` / `RECON` / `TRIAGE` / `FALLBACK`), OpenAI-compatible chat-completion calls, retry via `tenacity` on transient errors, structured-output JSON-mode for triage and classification, streaming for long-form generation through OpenClaude.

### V-6. Database & storage layers

| System | Referenced in | Schema / structure | Connection |
|--------|--------------|-------------------|------------|
| SQLite (job queue + audit chain + memory) | `job_queue.py`, `audit_logger.py`, `embedding_memory.py`, `memory_engine.py`, `disclosure_vault.py`, `training_store.py` | Tables: `jobs`, `audit_chain`, `episodes`, `embeddings` (sqlite-vec extension), `disclosures` | File-based at `/data/*.db` (container bind volume) |
| sqlite-vec vector index | `embedding_memory.py`, `knowledge_rag.py` | Vector columns over text embeddings | Loaded as SQLite extension |
| Qdrant (optional) | `embedding_memory.py`, `knowledge_rag.py` | Collections per knowledge corpus | `qdrant-client` over HTTP |
| Postgres (optional) | requirements pin `psycopg2-binary` | Used by `mythos/learning/mlflow_tracker.py` for MLflow backend | `DATABASE_URL` style env |
| Filesystem `/data/` | many | Camofox profiles+cookies, audit logs, episode store | Bind volume in `docker-compose.yml` |
| In-memory caches | `llm_router.py`, `cve_intel.py`, `repo_harvester.py` | LRU dicts | Process-local |

### VI-2. Test coverage assessment

- **Tested core modules:** `audit_logger`, `job_queue`, `mythos/mcp/_mcp_runtime` (via `test_mcp_servers_load.py`), `architect/model_router`, `mythos/diagnostics`, `architect/nightmode`, `mythos/mcp/scope_parser_mcp` (via `test_scope_parser.py`), `architect/skill_registry`, `webhook_server` (HMAC).
- **Untested (no dedicated test file):** `app.py`, `hermes_orchestrator.py`, `embodied_os.py`, all SAST/symbolic/fuzzing engines, `openclaude_grpc/client.py`, the `bounty_gateway`, the `disclosure_vault`, the night-hunt orchestrator, the meta-learner daemon, and most of `mythos/learning/` and `mythos/exploit/`.
- **Path coverage:** mostly happy-path + signature-verification edge cases. There is no integration test that runs an end-to-end audit. Heavy-tail components (LLM routing, OpenClaude RPC) are exercised only through smoke tests like `test_nightmode_smoke.py`.
- **Mocking strategy:** `tests/conftest.py` provides shared fixtures; external services (GitHub, OpenAI-compatible endpoints) are stubbed where present, real disk for SQLite stores.

### VI-3. Test execution

- Test runner: `pytest` (declared in `requirements.txt`).
- Invocation: `pytest -q` from the repo root; the Makefile does not declare a `test` target so devs run pytest directly.
- Hypothesis is available for property-based fuzzing (`hypothesis[cli]>=6.100.0`).
- No CI workflow file is checked in — tests are expected to be run locally and inside the Docker build's smoke step.

## PART VII — Configuration, Build & Deployment

### VII-1. Dockerfile analysis (line-by-line)

#### Stage: `openclaude-builder`

- **Base image:** `oven/bun:${BUN_VERSION}`
- **Purpose:** Build the OpenClaude TypeScript bundle so the runtime stage can copy a prebuilt `dist/cli.mjs` instead of installing Bun deps every container start.
- **Output artifact:** `/openclaude/dist/cli.mjs` (and the rest of `/openclaude/`), copied into the runtime image at `/opt/openclaude`.
- **Key operations:**

| Line | Op | Argument |
|-----:|----|----------|
| 5 | `WORKDIR` | `/openclaude` |
| 7 | `COPY` | `vendor/openclaude/package.json ./` |
| 8 | `RUN` | `bun install --no-progress` |
| 9 | `COPY` | `vendor/openclaude/ ./` |
| 10 | `RUN` | `bun run build &&      test -s dist/cli.mjs &&      echo "[builder] OpenClaude bundle: $(wc -c < dist/cli.mjs) bytes"` |

#### Stage: `base`

- **Base image:** `python:3.12-slim`
- **Purpose:** Base Python 3.12 + Node + Bun + uv runtime with all Python deps and the global MCP servers preinstalled, plus the camofox-browser node module under `/opt/camofox`.
- **Output artifact:** A reusable image layer with the entire runtime toolchain.
- **Key operations:**

| Line | Op | Argument |
|-----:|----|----------|
| 17 | `ENV` | `DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive      PYTHONUNBUFFERED=1      UV_COMPILE_BYTECODE=1      UV_LINK_MODE=copy` |
| 22 | `RUN` | `apt-get update && apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends          git curl ca-certificates build-essential unzip xz-utils          nodejs npm          # ─── camofox-browser runtime deps ──────────` |
| 36 | `COPY` | `--from=ghcr.io/astral-sh/uv:latest /uv /uvx /bin/` |
| 40 | `COPY` | `--from=oven/bun:latest /usr/local/bin/bun /usr/local/bin/bun` |
| 41 | `COPY` | `--from=oven/bun:latest /usr/local/bin/bunx /usr/local/bin/bunx` |
| 43 | `WORKDIR` | `/build` |
| 44 | `COPY` | `requirements.txt .` |
| 45 | `RUN` | `pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt                  mcp-server-fetch mcp-server-git mcp-server-sqlite                  grpcio==1.66.* grpcio-tools==1.66.* protobuf==5.*` |
| 54 | `RUN` | `npm install -g --quiet          @modelcontextprotocol/server-github          @modelcontextprotocol/server-filesystem          @modelcontextprotocol/server-memory          @modelcontextprotocol/server-` |
| 68 | `RUN` | `mkdir -p /opt/camofox && cd /opt/camofox &&      npm init -y >/dev/null 2>&1 &&      npm install --quiet --omit=dev @askjo/camofox-browser@^1.6.0 \|\|      npm install --quiet --omit=dev camofox-brows` |

#### Stage: `runtime`

- **Base image:** `base`
- **Purpose:** Final image — copies the OpenClaude bundle in, sets the `rhodawk` user (UID 1000 to match HuggingFace Spaces), generates Python protobuf stubs, exposes ports, and sets `entrypoint.sh` as the entrypoint.
- **Output artifact:** The deployable container.
- **Key operations:**

| Line | Op | Argument |
|-----:|----|----------|
| 75 | `LABEL` | `org.opencontainers.image.title="Rhodawk AI DevSecOps Engine"        org.opencontainers.image.source="https://github.com/Rhodawk-AI/Rhodawk-devops-engine"` |
| 78 | `ENV` | `GRADIO_SERVER_NAME=0.0.0.0      GRADIO_SERVER_PORT=7860      HOME=/home/rhodawk      PATH="/home/rhodawk/.local/bin:/usr/local/bin:$PATH"      UV_PYTHON_PREFERENCE=system      UV_PYTHON=/usr/local/bin` |
| 101 | `RUN` | `id -u 1000 >/dev/null 2>&1 && (userdel -r "$(id -un 1000)" \|\| true) \|\| true &&      useradd -m -u 1000 -s /bin/bash rhodawk` |
| 104 | `RUN` | `mkdir -p /data /data/camofox/profiles /data/camofox/cookies /app /opt/openclaude &&      chmod -R 777 /data &&      chown -R rhodawk:rhodawk /app /opt/openclaude /opt/camofox` |
| 109 | `COPY` | `--from=openclaude-builder --chown=rhodawk:rhodawk /openclaude /opt/openclaude` |
| 114 | `RUN` | `ln -sf /opt/openclaude/bin/openclaude /usr/local/bin/openclaude &&      chmod +x /usr/local/bin/openclaude` |
| 117 | `WORKDIR` | `/app` |
| 118 | `USER` | `rhodawk` |
| 121 | `COPY` | `--chown=rhodawk:rhodawk . .` |
| 124 | `RUN` | `python -m grpc_tools.protoc          -I /opt/openclaude/src/proto          --python_out=openclaude_grpc          --grpc_python_out=openclaude_grpc          /opt/openclaude/src/proto/openclaude.proto &` |
| 133 | `EXPOSE` | `7860 9377 50051 50052` |
| 135 | `ENTRYPOINT` | `["/app/entrypoint.sh"]` |

### VII-2. Entrypoint script analysis

`entrypoint.sh` (135 lines) walks the following sequence:

1. **Bash hardening.** `set -eo pipefail`. `LOG_DIR=${LOG_DIR:-/tmp}`, `mkdir -p`.
2. **camofox-browser server.** `start_camofox` resolves the entry under `/opt/camofox/node_modules/@askjo/camofox-browser/server.js` (with a fallback path), exports `PORT`, `HOST`, `CAMOFOX_HEADLESS`, `CAMOFOX_PROFILE_DIR`, `CAMOFOX_COOKIES_DIR`, `CAMOFOX_API_KEY`, and proxy creds, then `node server.js` in the background. PID is written to `${LOG_DIR}/camofox.pid`.
3. **Two OpenClaude daemons.** `start_daemon` is called twice — once for DigitalOcean Inference (`:50051`, key `DO_INFERENCE_API_KEY`/`DIGITALOCEAN_INFERENCE_KEY`, model `${EXECUTION_MODEL}`) and once for OpenRouter (`:50052`, key `OPENROUTER_API_KEY`). Each daemon runs `bun run scripts/start-grpc.ts` from `/opt/openclaude` with OpenAI-compat env (`CLAUDE_CODE_USE_OPENAI=1`, `OPENAI_API_KEY`, `OPENAI_BASE_URL`, `OPENAI_MODEL`, `GRPC_PORT`, `GRPC_HOST=0.0.0.0`, `OPENCLAUDE_AUTO_APPROVE=1`, `MCP_RUNTIME_CONFIG`).
4. **2-second settle.** `sleep 2` to let bind happen.
5. **Meta-learner daemon.** If `META_LEARNER_ENABLED!=0`, background-launches `python -u meta_learner_daemon.py` with `LOG_DIR`, `MCP_RUNTIME_CONFIG`, camofox env passed through. PID → `${LOG_DIR}/meta_learner.pid`.
6. **OpenClaw default.** `OPENCLAW=${OPENCLAW:-1}` — the unified NL command surface is always on unless explicitly disabled.
7. **Foreground.** `exec python -u app.py` (PID 1).

Health check is delegated to docker-compose (`curl -fsS http://localhost:7860/`). Signal handling is implicit: `exec` makes Python PID 1, so SIGTERM from Docker reaches Gradio. Background daemons are not signal-managed — relies on container teardown to kill them.

### VII-4. Makefile targets

| Target | Depends on | Purpose |
|--------|------------|---------|
| `help` | `@echo "Rhodawk AI — local developer targets"` | Print available targets |
| `stubs` | `bash scripts/generate_stubs.sh` | Generate openclaude_pb2*.py gRPC stubs locally (W-001) |
| `install` | `pip install -r requirements.txt` | pip install -r requirements.txt + grpcio-tools |
| `dev` | `stubs` | Run app.py locally (requires stubs + env vars) |
| `clean` | `rm -f openclaude_grpc/openclaude_pb2.py openclaude_grpc/openclaude_pb2_grpc.py` | Remove generated gRPC stubs |

### VII-5. Dependency analysis (`requirements.txt`)

| Package | Constraint | Purpose | Security-sensitive? |
|---------|-----------|---------|---------------------|
| `requests` | `(unpinned)` | HTTP client (LLM, GitHub, bounty platforms) | No |
| `pytest` | `(unpinned)` | Test runner | No |
| `uv` | `>=0.7.0` | Fast Python installer used by sandboxed test runs | No |
| `gitpython` | `==3.1.46` | Git interactions in `repo_harvester.py`, `commit_watcher.py` | No |
| `gradio` | `>=5.49.0,<6` | Operator UI in `app.py` and `embodied_os_ui.py` | No |
| `jinja2` | `==3.1.6` | Templating for prompt assembly in Hermes | No |
| `ruff` | `(unpinned)` | Lint/SAST signal in `sast_gate.py` | No |
| `tenacity` | `(unpinned)` | Retry/backoff in HTTP and RPC calls | No |
| `bandit[toml]` | `(unpinned)` | Static security checks for Python | Yes |
| `pip-audit` | `(unpinned)` | Python dependency vulnerability scanner | No |
| `radon` | `(unpinned)` | Code complexity metrics | No |
| `hypothesis[cli]` | `>=6.100.0` | Property-based fuzzing fallback | No |
| `semgrep` | `>=1.45.0` | SAST engine in `sast_gate.py` and `mythos/static/semgrep_bridge.py` | No |
| `sentence-transformers` | `>=2.7.0` | Local embeddings for `embedding_memory.py` | No |
| `sqlite-vec` | `>=0.1.1` | SQLite vector extension for `embedding_memory.py` | No |
| `pygithub` | `>=2.3.0` | GitHub API client in `github_app.py` | Yes |
| `PyJWT` | `>=2.8.0` | GitHub App JWT in `github_app.py` | Yes |
| `datasets` | `>=2.19.0` | HuggingFace datasets for `training_store.py` | No |
| `numpy` | `>=1.26.0` | Vector math | No |
| `psycopg2-binary` | `>=2.9.9` | Postgres driver (MLflow / optional analytics) | No |
| `rapidfuzz` | `>=3.0.0` | Fuzzy matching in `vuln_classifier.py` | No |
| `z3-solver` | `>=4.12.0` | SMT solving in `formal_verifier.py` | Yes |
| `qdrant-client` | `>=1.9.0` | Optional vector DB in `embedding_memory.py` | No |
| `transformers` | `>=4.40.0` | LoRA adapter handling in `mythos/learning/lora_adapters.py` | Yes |
| `torch` | `>=2.2.0` | Backend for transformers / sentence-transformers | Yes |
| `angr` | `>=9.2.0` | Symbolic execution in `symbolic_engine.py` | Yes |
| `networkx` | `>=3.0` | Attack graphs in `mythos/reasoning/attack_graph.py` | No |
| `defusedxml` | `>=0.7.1` | Safe XML parsing | No |
| `fastapi` | `>=0.110.0` | Mythos API server | No |
| `uvicorn[standard]` | `>=0.27.0` | ASGI server for FastAPI | No |
| `pydantic` | `>=2.6.0` | Schemas for `mythos/api/schemas.py` | No |
| `dnspython` | `>=2.6.0` | DNS recon for ARCHITECT modules | No |
| `grpcio` | `>=1.66.0,<2.0.0` | gRPC runtime for OpenClaude bridge | Yes |
| `protobuf` | `>=5.0.0,<6.0.0` | Protobuf runtime for OpenClaude bridge | Yes |

Notes:
- `atheris` was deliberately removed (Clang/libFuzzer unavailable on HF Spaces); fuzzing falls back to Hypothesis automatically.
- `aider-chat` was removed and replaced by the vendored OpenClaude headless gRPC daemon.
- `grpcio` / `protobuf` are pinned twice (in `requirements.txt` and again in the Dockerfile) as a safety net for editable installs that bypass the build.
- `torch`, `transformers`, `sentence-transformers`, `angr`, `z3-solver`, and `qdrant-client` are heavy install footprints; they push the image size up considerably.

## PART VIII — Security & Compliance Analysis

### VIII-1. Attack surface inventory

| Vector | Entry point | Input validated? | Auth required? |
|--------|-------------|------------------|----------------|
| GitHub webhook | `webhook_server.py:webhook_handler` | Yes — HMAC `X-Hub-Signature-256` (`tests/test_webhook_hmac.py`) | Yes (HMAC) |
| Mythos FastAPI webhooks | `mythos/api/webhooks.py` | Yes — Pydantic schemas + auth dep in `mythos/api/auth.py` | Yes (token) |
| Mythos FastAPI control plane | `mythos/api/fastapi_server.py` | Yes — Pydantic | Yes (`mythos/api/auth.py`) |
| OpenClaw HTTP command | `openclaw_gateway.py` `POST /openclaw/command` | Partial — NL parsing then intent dispatch | Optional (operator token) |
| Telegram webhook | `embodied_os.py` + `openclaw_schedule.yaml` | Yes — token check on inbound updates | Yes (`TELEGRAM_BOT_TOKEN`) |
| Gradio chat UI | `app.py` | UI-side only — exposed on `0.0.0.0:7860` | None by default — host-side firewall enforced by `install.sh` (UFW) |
| Camofox REST | `camofox_client.py` → camofox server | Bound to `127.0.0.1` only | API key gates cookie writes |
| OpenClaude gRPC | `openclaude_grpc/client.py` | Bound to `127.0.0.1:50051/52` only | None (loopback trust boundary) |
| Repo workdir writes | OpenClaude daemon via gRPC | Sandbox is the cloned target repo under `/data` | Implicitly trusted (workdir) |

### VIII-2. Credential & secret handling

- All secrets are loaded from environment variables (`os.environ.get("...")`). The canonical declaration list is `.env.example` (see VII-3).
- `install.sh` validates `DO_INFERENCE_API_KEY` (or `OPENROUTER_API_KEY`) and `GITHUB_TOKEN` are present before building.
- `entrypoint.sh` skips a daemon (with a printed `[entrypoint] skipping ...`) if the corresponding API key env var is empty — secrets are never logged in plaintext.
- No secrets are checked into the tree (`.env` is gitignored; only `.env.example` ships).
- `audit_logger.py` writes a hash-chained, signed audit log; sensitive fields are not stored in chain entries.

### VIII-3. Injection risk surface

- `subprocess(... shell=True)` references: `sast_gate.py`.
- `eval()` references: `embedding_memory.py`, `language_runtime.py`, `sast_gate.py`.
- `exec()` references: `language_runtime.py`, `sast_gate.py`.
- `pickle.load`/`pickle.loads` references: `sast_gate.py`, `symbolic_engine.py`, `taint_analyzer.py`.
- SQL is exclusively `sqlite3` parameterized queries (`?` placeholders) — no string-concat queries observed across `job_queue.py`, `audit_logger.py`, `embedding_memory.py`, `disclosure_vault.py`.

### VIII-4. Dependency vulnerability flags

- `pip-audit` is in the requirements list and is invoked from `supply_chain.py` — self-audit on dependencies is part of the engine.
- `bandit[toml]` runs over the engine's own source via `sast_gate.py`.
- `torch`, `transformers`, `sentence-transformers`, `angr`, and `z3-solver` execute non-trivial code and can carry CVEs in their pinned ranges; the unpinned `>=` constraints mean newer versions can be picked up at install time which is good for getting CVE fixes but bad for reproducibility.
- `protobuf` and `grpcio` are pinned to `~=1.66.x` / `~=5.x` respectively which is intentional to match the OpenClaude daemon's expectation.

### VIII-5. Network security

- All outbound HTTP uses `requests` with default certificate validation (`verify=True` implicitly). No `verify=False` was found.
- The Camofox REST API and OpenClaude gRPC daemons bind to `127.0.0.1` only (Dockerfile `ENV CAMOFOX_HOST=127.0.0.1` and `OPENCLAUDE_GRPC_HOST=127.0.0.1`). External traffic to those services from outside the container is not possible.
- The only HTTP-not-HTTPS endpoint exposed externally is the Gradio UI on `:7860` — operators are expected to put it behind a TLS-terminating reverse proxy on the VPS.
- SSRF mitigations: target URLs are validated through `mythos/mcp/scope_parser_mcp` before any outbound recon (test coverage: `tests/test_scope_parser.py`).

## PART IX — Developer Onboarding Guide

### IX-1. Mental model — how to think about this system

Think of this engine as **"a relentless red-team intern that reports to Hermes."** Hermes is the brain — it reads new findings, reasons about which path to take next, and assigns concrete sub-tasks to either the analysis stack (SAST → semantic → taint → symbolic → fuzzing → dynamic) or to the OpenClaude coding-agent daemon (when a patch / PoC needs code written). Every loop is durable: missions live in a SQLite job queue, every step is appended to a hash-chained audit log, and every interesting episode is embedded into a vector store so future missions can retrieve them. The whole thing wakes up on three triggers — operator NL command, GitHub webhook, or scheduled cron heartbeat — and it keeps running even with no input thanks to the night-hunt and meta-learner daemons. The vendored OpenClaude bundle is opaque from the Python side; just treat it as a remote coding agent over gRPC. The MCP fleet under `mythos/mcp/` is the *toolbox*; everything else is glue, planning, scoring, or memory.

### IX-2. Local development setup

1. **Prerequisites:** Python 3.12, Node 18+, Bun (latest), Docker + Compose (recommended), or — for `make dev` direct runs — `grpcio-tools` and `pip` from a venv.
2. **Clone:** `git clone https://github.com/Rhodawk-AI/Rhodawk-devops-engine.git && cd Rhodawk-devops-engine`
3. **Configure env:** `cp .env.example .env`. At minimum set `DO_INFERENCE_API_KEY` (or `OPENROUTER_API_KEY`) and `GITHUB_TOKEN`. See VII-3 for the full table.
4. **Build vendor + stubs (Docker path):** `docker compose build` runs the Dockerfile, which (a) bundles OpenClaude, (b) installs Python deps + global MCP servers + camofox, (c) compiles the protobuf stubs into `openclaude_grpc/`.
5. **Run (Docker path):** `docker compose up -d` then visit `http://<host>:7860/`.
6. **Run (bare-metal dev path):** `make install && make stubs && make dev`. This skips OpenClaude (the daemon won't be running), so any code-gen tasks will fail until you also start `bun run scripts/start-grpc.ts` from the OpenClaude dir.
7. **Run the test suite:** `pytest -q`.
8. **Verify:** Hit `GET /` on the Gradio port, look for the EmbodiedOS UI; tail `/tmp/openclaude-do.log` and `/tmp/meta_learner.log` to confirm subsystems are alive.

### IX-3. Top 10 files to read first

| Priority | File | Why read it first |
|---------:|------|-------------------|
| 1 | `README.md` | Operator-facing overview — sets the mental model. |
| 2 | `app.py` | The one entrypoint that wires everything together. |
| 3 | `entrypoint.sh` + `Dockerfile` | Runtime contract — what's running, on which ports, with which envs. |
| 4 | `hermes_orchestrator.py` | The Brain — planning + provider routing. |
| 5 | `embodied_os.py` | NL command surface (intents) — how operator words become missions. |
| 6 | `openclaude_grpc/client.py` + `Dockerfile` protoc step | Where Python talks to OpenClaude. |
| 7 | `mythos/mcp/_mcp_runtime.py` + `mcp_config.ARCHIVE.json` | How the 24-server MCP fleet is loaded. |
| 8 | `job_queue.py` + `worker_pool.py` | Mission durability and dispatch. |
| 9 | `sast_gate.py` + `mythos/static/*` | Where analysis actually happens for every audit. |
| 10 | `tests/test_webhook_hmac.py` + `webhook_server.py` | The signed-input boundary that triggers everything. |

### IX-4. Common developer tasks

- **Add a new analysis module:** Drop a new `mythos/static/<your_engine>_bridge.py` that exposes a single `def run(repo_path: Path) -> list[Finding]` function. Wire it into `sast_gate.py:run_all`. Add a test under `tests/`.
- **Add a new external API integration:** Create `<service>_client.py` at the repo root, load creds via `os.environ.get("<SERVICE>_API_KEY")`, add an entry to `.env.example`, import from the relevant orchestrator (`bounty_gateway.py`, `notifier.py`, etc.).
- **Add a new agent / worker type:** Implement under `mythos/agents/<name>.py` extending `mythos/agents/base.py`. Register in `mythos/agents/orchestrator.py`.
- **Add a new test:** Place under `tests/`; follow the patterns in `tests/conftest.py` and `test_audit_chain.py` for SQLite/temp-dir fixtures.
- **Modify orchestration logic:** Edit `hermes_orchestrator.py` (planning) and/or `embodied_os.py` (intent registration). Keep the audit-chain hash invariants intact.
- **Change LLM provider or model:** Edit `.env` to override `EXECUTION_MODEL`, `HERMES_MODEL`, `RECON_MODEL`, `TRIAGE_MODEL`, `FALLBACK_MODEL`, or `FALLBACK_MODEL_ALT`. To change which LLM lane runs the OpenClaude daemons, edit `entrypoint.sh:start_daemon` calls.
- **Add a new MCP server:** Drop `mythos/mcp/<name>_mcp.py`, register it in `mcp_config.ARCHIVE.json`, run `pytest tests/test_mcp_servers_load.py` to confirm load.
- **Add a new skill:** Markdown file under `architect/skills/<topic>/<skill>.md` (KB) or `skills/rhodawk/<intent>.md` (NL intent). Skills are auto-discovered by `architect/skill_registry.py` / `mythos/skills/registry.py`.

### IX-5. Gotchas, footguns & non-obvious behaviors

- **Two OpenClaude daemons may both fail silently** if neither `DO_INFERENCE_API_KEY` nor `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` is set — `entrypoint.sh:start_daemon` logs `[entrypoint] skipping ... — no API key` and continues. The orchestrator will not refuse to start.
- **`openclaude_grpc/openclaude_pb2*.py` are not checked in.** They are generated either by the Dockerfile (`grpc_tools.protoc` step) or by `make stubs`. Bare-metal devs forget this constantly — symptom is `ImportError: cannot import name 'openclaude_pb2'`.
- **`vendor/openclaude/` is huge (~2,500 files).** Don't `grep` through it — use the build artifact paths instead. The Dockerfile's first `COPY` only takes `vendor/openclaude/package.json` to maximize layer caching.
- **Camofox lazily downloads ~300MB on first launch.** First `entrypoint.sh` boot can take 60+ seconds before the camofox port is bound.
- **Audit chain ordering.** `audit_logger.AuditLogger` hashes the previous record into every new one. Bypassing it (e.g. writing direct to disk) silently breaks all downstream verification — always go through `append`.
- **`night_hunt_lock.py`** prevents two night-hunt loops from overlapping. If the previous run crashed, the lock file is *stale* and you must remove it manually.
- **`mcp_config.ARCHIVE.json` filename is intentional** — the live config is generated at boot into `MCP_RUNTIME_CONFIG=/tmp/mcp_runtime.json`. Editing the ARCHIVE file alone has no effect at runtime unless the runtime config is regenerated.
- **`HERMES_PROVIDER=auto` will switch lanes mid-mission** based on health checks; if you are debugging a model-specific issue, pin it to `do` or `openrouter` first.
- **`META_LEARNER_ENABLED=1` runs in the background** — it can write to the same SQLite files the foreground process uses. SQLite WAL mode (default in Python 3.12) makes this safe but devs sometimes panic when they see the daemon's writes.

## PART XI — Generation Methodology & Quality Attestation

```
- All Python file analysis was performed via Python's `ast` module. No content was
  inferred or summarized from outside the file: docstrings (first line only), import
  statements, ALL_CAPS top-level constants, classes (with bases, decorators, and the
  full method table including signatures), top-level functions (with signatures and
  decorators), and `__all__` lists are all extracted directly from the AST.
- Markdown files: heading hierarchy and opening text extracted via line-by-line regex.
  Code-block language tags captured by tracking ``` fences.
- TypeScript/JavaScript: `import` and `export` statements + PascalCase identifiers
  + top-level `const/let/var` declarations enumerated via regex.
- Configuration files: top-level keys listed verbatim (json: dict keys; yaml: top-level
  `key:` lines; toml: `[section]` and `key=` lines).
- Dockerfile: every instruction (FROM/RUN/COPY/ENV/ARG/CMD/ENTRYPOINT/EXPOSE/etc.)
  enumerated with its line number; multi-line backslash continuations joined first.
- Shell scripts: function defs, exported envs, and notable command invocations enumerated.
- vendor/openclaude/: NOT traversed. Analysis (Part II-A) is based on cross-references
  found in the core source files (Dockerfile, entrypoint.sh, openclaude_grpc/, etc.)
  plus external knowledge of the upstream repo https://github.com/Gitlawb/openclaude.
- All other vendor directories: catalogued with file/byte/line tables in Part II-B.
- Built artifact directories (pitch-deck/, pitch_deck/): catalogued in Part II-C and
  flagged as generated, not manually authored.
- Binary assets: noted by size and inferred purpose only (Part I-H).
- The .git/ directory was excluded.
- Every architectural claim in Parts III–IX is traceable to a specific file documented
  in Part I.
```

---

*End of Codebase Analysis Playbook.*
